  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText2625081452656553489" style="display:none">Viana, la única hija del duque de Rocagrís, está prometida al joven Robian de Castelmar desde que ambos eran niños. Los dos se aman y se casarán en primavera. Sin embargo, durante los festejos del solsticio de invierno, un arisco montaraz advierte al rey de Nortia y sus caballeros de la amenaza de los bárbaros de las estepas... y tanto Robian como el duque se ven obligados a marchar a la guerra. En tales circunstancias, una doncella como Viana no puede hacer otra cosa que esperar su regreso... y, tal vez, prestar atención a las leyendas que se cuentan sobre el Gran Bosque... el lugar donde los árboles cantan.</span>

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1242193-la-verdad-el-libro-es-malo-no-entiendo">La verdad el libro es malo, no entiendo, como tiene tanto rating ni porque tiene tantos comentarios positivos? La protagonista es bastante estupida y lerda de razonamiento, bastante lela. Hay partes que son tan obvias y la muy lela hace todo lo que sea necesario para ponerse en peligro, para que la atrapen, etc... Siempre pasa lo mismo, autoras que hacen personajes femeninos con reraso mental es el mayor cliche.</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/8292133-eddard-hordas">Eddard Hordas</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Concuerdo en parte contigo. No es un super libro, pero tampoco es un basura. Pero tienes razón: tuvo mucha publicidad, honestamente me esperaba algo m<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Concuerdo en parte contigo. No es un super libro, pero tampoco es un basura. Pero tienes razón: tuvo mucha publicidad, honestamente me esperaba algo más impresionante; pero resultó siendo una novela casi adolescente. Aun así no dejo de confiar en que Gallego pueda escribir una novela que realmente valga la pena. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2263086672" />
    <a title="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44480390-jules-witchyrover"><img alt="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578182465p2/44480390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2263086672?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jules ♈  (witchyrover)" href="/user/show/44480390-jules-witchyrover">Jules ♈  (witchyrover)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263086672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer236892037084710748">I remember that I loved this book. It was even one of the first books that brought me to tears. What I do remember was that the main character was annoying and her excuses had no fundament. However life and fate hit her against a brick wall and eventually she learned that the world is not full of rainbows. I would like to re read it again in the future to see if my opinion still stands. <br/><br/><b> Spanish translation </b><br/>Recuerdo que amé este libro. Incluso fue uno de los primeros que me hizo llorar a mares. </span>
  <span id="freeText236892037084710748" style="display:none">I remember that I loved this book. It was even one of the first books that brought me to tears. What I do remember was that the main character was annoying and her excuses had no fundament. However life and fate hit her against a brick wall and eventually she learned that the world is not full of rainbows. I would like to re read it again in the future to see if my opinion still stands. <br /><br /><b> Spanish translation </b><br />Recuerdo que amé este libro. Incluso fue uno de los primeros que me hizo llorar a mares. Lo que recuerdo era que el personaje principal era insoportable y sus excusas no tenían fundamento. Aun así, la vida y el destino le pegaron contra una pared de ladrillos y eventualmente aprendió que la vida no es color de rosa. Me encantaría volverlo a leer en el futuro para ver si mi opinión sigue siendo la misma.</span>
  <a data-text-id="236892037084710748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2252150799?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivanna" href="/user/show/76303541-ivanna">Ivanna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2252150799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12804896929808328541">I never liked to read, I never thought of opening this book. My older sister loves to read basically we have a library in the house of all the books that she read. She always recommends me this book, I saw how she cried, how she laughed and then how she read it again because she said it was incredible. It happened years until one day I saw it and decided I was going to read it, for some reason it called me a lot of attention, I started to read it and I wasn’t disappointed of nothing, the book wa</span>
  <span id="freeText12804896929808328541" style="display:none">I never liked to read, I never thought of opening this book. My older sister loves to read basically we have a library in the house of all the books that she read. She always recommends me this book, I saw how she cried, how she laughed and then how she read it again because she said it was incredible. It happened years until one day I saw it and decided I was going to read it, for some reason it called me a lot of attention, I started to read it and I wasn’t disappointed of nothing, the book was amazing. It is a book that is in the times of XVII and XVIII, and it is about a girl called Viana, she is the only daughter of the duke and she is supposed to marry a man named Robian. Something happens that nobody in the castle ever imagined, the war occurs, and all men are going to fight while Viana could not do anything because she was a woman.<br />This book charms me because it shows how a woman can defend and fight for what she wants, it shows you that women are courageous, and we can do more than what men think. Something very curious about this is that it gives rise to a magical world, that’s why it has the name "where the trees sing" that place according to the book is a fantastic world and there are many incredible characters, where Viana finds her true love. <br />You really cannot regret this book, when I start reading it I didn’t want it to end, I cried, I laughed and I wanted to read it again, definitely one of my favorite books, now I understand my sister.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1956919233614181122">3,5 stars rounded up<br/><br/>This book has been on my shelf for quite a few years and finally I was in the right mood to read it.   <span id="freeText1956919233614181122" style="display:none">3,5 stars rounded up<br /><br />This book has been on my shelf for quite a few years and finally I was in the right mood to read it. I enjoyed it, especially the medieval-like setting and all the wonderful descriptions of the forest, both the magical and non-magical parts of it. The story itself was quite simple and the main character was simultaneously reckless and naive, but it managed to engage me well enough.<br /><br />At times, it actually reminded me of Robin Hood's tale but just some elements, and the story was obviously original. It's just the similar atmosphere :) I very much like books set in a medieval-like setting but with fantasy elements, so it was a nice read for me, plus I liked how the last chapter wrapped it all up.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3407100820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3407100820" />
    <a title="Clara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93205648-clara"><img alt="Clara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564677212p2/93205648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3407100820?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clara" href="/user/show/93205648-clara">Clara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/93205648-clara?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3407100820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6741018793146856667">This book reads like a fairy tale... and I really liked it!<br/><br/>First of all, can we talk about how beautiful this book is? I loved the presentation: the drawings, the chapter pages presenting what is to come without (too many) spoilers, just enough to keep the reader interested. It gave a few spoilers at the beginning, but it was not problematic since the content could be guessed from the back cover. The way this book was presented really enhanced the story and helped me to dive into a magical story</span>
  <span id="freeText6741018793146856667" style="display:none">This book reads like a fairy tale... and I really liked it!<br /><br />First of all, can we talk about how beautiful this book is? I loved the presentation: the drawings, the chapter pages presenting what is to come without (too many) spoilers, just enough to keep the reader interested. It gave a few spoilers at the beginning, but it was not problematic since the content could be guessed from the back cover. The way this book was presented really enhanced the story and helped me to dive into a magical story full of "caballeros" and "princesas". <br /><br />The story in itself was rather enjoyable even though quite predictable. Everything we need to know to understand is told right at the beginning through Oki's tale during the reception, and the outcome of the war is no surprise given Lobo's warnings. But this is not when the story picks up. <br />Our main character, Viana, is the perfect princess: beautiful, kind, smart, and in love with the perfect prince. But her world is going to shatter with the outcome of the war and everything she thought she knew is going to come undone. From her situation, to her future. She first appears as a naive and helpless princess who relies on other people to survive, up until the end of the first part. But she is going to grow into a strong and pig-headed character who only acts according to her will, not following orders, sometimes for the best, most of the time for the worst. <br />I really liked following her, and watch her become this badass character she didn't know she could become. She was not the stupid "i-do-what-i-want" character but someone with a drive, with plans, and with reasons to act the way she did. Most of her actions go awry, but that's the beauty of it: even though nothing unravels the way she wants, we can't blame her for her actions. They bring positivity and negativity, and (apart for the first time she really messed up) it was not that much her fault. It can also be excused through the fact that she was a princess for such a long time that she doesn't have the hindsight to properly prepare her expeditions. <br /><br />I particularly liked Lobo and his relationship with Viana and, especially, how he was not duped by her and could see right through her mind and her actions. His stories about his ear that was cut off and how he learned two things about it were hilarious and I really enjoyed reading about it. I wanted to shake him so badly and tell him to listen to Viana's "crazy" hypothesis but him not believing her is understandable, even more so when we consider her being 16 or 17 at the time. <br /><br />I particularly liked Robin. He appears as the coward who betrays everyone, but his actions were driven and, once again, understandable. He was a quite complex character who, on one side, agrees to be a coward and a joke for the sake of saving his family, and on the other side struggle with the wish to make amends and regain his reputation. He betrayed Viana, and yet sacrifices his own gain by not delivering her to the "barbaros". I really empathised with him, contrary to what Viana is trying to make us think.<br /><br />I really love this story; however, one of the biggest criticism I could make is how one-sided and not fleshed out characters are. They seem really simple and there to serve one purpose, and did not make me feel that much (Uri is not that complex, and his mystery easily solvable once we get more information about his people, Dorea is only there for maternal love, etc.). Had the characters been more human, and the bad guys less cardboard copies of Disney villains, I think I would've liked it better. Yet, I cannot really blame this book as it was published in a time when the book fashion was to have those kind of characters (if I'm not wrong) and it is acceptable for this type of story. <br /><br />This was already a re-read, and it probably won't be the last!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6741018793146856667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14153092233281584586" style="display:none">Viana of Rocagrís, is the protagonist of this fantasy novel. She’s a shy girl, in love with love. That, one day, has to forget everything what she knows of be a high Lady of Nortia. She was engaged to Robian, who makes the wrong decision when the barbarians invade Nortia and Harak takes the throne of the kingdom.<br />Viana, wasn’t the suffer girl of a tragic story, she was really annoying at the beginning, but the change a lot when she met Lobo, and he immediately try to teach her how to fight and have voice (something that wasn’t common in a high Lady as her). However, the real problem is when she tries to do things for her own and bring many problems to people surround her. She really doesn't think very much, she just do everything what she thinks it's ok and expect de best result or someone who save her.<br /><br />I give three of five stars; I think the first chapters are boring. <b> Sorry! :/ </b><br /><br />I think the author didn’t develop a little more the fantasy world that she was trying to create and it makes more interesting the story.</span>

  <span id="freeText8489530082362082667" style="display:none">First, the good things: The narration is good and everything that happens in the forest is super interesting, i loved how creative the inside of the forest was once we got there. Urie was my favorite and Oki reminded me of Snufkin from Moomins. <br /><br />That being said....<br /><br />The first part of the book is boring. Theres no way around it. I almost stopped reading entirely; not only it becomes dull and everytime you think the story will take you someplace interesting it leads you to something worse, the protagonist for the better part of the story is just /there/. I guess Gallego was trying to show how much she changes from the start to the end but this only hurts Viana as a character, she doesnt have anything you can recognize as "hers" except how many bad decisions she makes over and over again.<br /><br />You'd think the trees and the forest would be the focus once you get outside the kingdom, but no.<br />The most interesting part of the book takes 2-3 chapters, the most creative stuff is barely explored.<br />I see the potencial there and Im sad we didnt get that. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392823537" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14554800931551951700">This book left me speechless.. i don't think i'll be able to find the right words to describe this book.<br/>It is beautiful and made me really emotional.. sometimes angry or excited, exasperated because the main character did something incredibly stupid again, hopeful that everything would turn out well in the end, sad because of the story and finally because i finished the book. The main character Viana was sometimes very annoying but i like how the author allowed her to mature with the progress of</span>
  <span id="freeText14554800931551951700" style="display:none">This book left me speechless.. i don't think i'll be able to find the right words to describe this book.<br />It is beautiful and made me really emotional.. sometimes angry or excited, exasperated because the main character did something incredibly stupid again, hopeful that everything would turn out well in the end, sad because of the story and finally because i finished the book. The main character Viana was sometimes very annoying but i like how the author allowed her to mature with the progress of the story and i liked how the things she had to go trough changed her forever and showed in her character. She had her faults and her plans didn't go always as planned and i like the contrast between the damsel in distress and the woman she turned out to be later in the book when she took the matters in her own hand.<br />This was already the second book from Laura Gallego that made me cry like a baby (the first was Todos los hadas). Her style has visibly matured and her books have now a deepness that i sometimes missed in her earlier works. I hope to see a lot of similar touching works from her in the future. (Maybe in the same universe than this book?)</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ifl+nE9Oz67juCXrlRsB+EAy9fxAdlHAIdt2LXoNobSz3xdO9BAGxkSTkYpi7gsnlm0SNI7736d6pTCct05TLg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a">About Laura Gallego García</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1398792330p3/228898.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a">Laura Gallego García
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6364485931736579644">Laura Gallego García is a Spanish author of fantasy and children's books. She studied Spanish Philology at the University of Valencia, and is currently working on her doctoral thesis. <br/><br/>Her first novel, at the age of 21, was published because she won the Barco de Vapor literature prize and still is one of her most recognizable works: Finis Mundi. After that, her now stablished literary career began.</span>
  <span id="freeText6364485931736579644" style="display:none">Laura Gallego García is a Spanish author of fantasy and children's books. She studied Spanish Philology at the University of Valencia, and is currently working on her doctoral thesis. <br /><br />Her first novel, at the age of 21, was published because she won the Barco de Vapor literature prize and still is one of her most recognizable works: Finis Mundi. After that, her now stablished literary career began. <br /><br />Finis Mundi was followed, chronologically, by (only mentioning the ones that achieved notable popularity)the ''Crónicas de la Torre'' saga, ''The Legend of the Wandering King'', ''Memories of Idhún'' saga, ''La Emperatriz de los Etéreos'' and the ''Alas Negras'' saga. <br />From all of them, her most popular and internationally recognized work has been the Memorias de Idhún saga. Formed by three books, written between 2004 and 2006, the story (pure fantasy genre) centers in the three main characters: Victoria, Jack and Christian; and the world of Idhún. Dragons, unicorns, magic, prophecies and everything your imagination can lead you to. <br />The saga of Idhún and most of her works have been published to numerous languagues such as English, French, German, Italian, Hungarian, Greek, Portuguese, Corean, Polish, Swedish, Finish, Danish, Rumanian, Turkish...<br /><br />She loves manga comics. Her favourite book of all time is ''The Neverending Story'', though she enjoys reading as well authors such as Tolkien, Weis, Peter Beagle and Coehlo.<br /><br />Currently she combines being a mother and enjoying her family life with the realization of her thesis. She finished this year her last novel, ''Donde los árboles cantan'' (Where the trees sing), which will be published in October 2011. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6364485931736579644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
